[31m--[ [0m[34mMatch #[0m[33m114[0m[34m of [0m[33m516[0m[31m ]--[0m
   Rule Id: [34mBD000701[0m
       Tag: [34mSecurity.Backdoor.DataExfiltration.Token[0m
  Severity: [36mImportant[0m, Confidence: [36mHigh[0m

   Pattern: [32m(npm owner|password|htpasswd|auth_?token|secret_?key|private_?key|authorized_keys?|npmrc|\.ssh|usersecrets?|api_?keys|nuget\.config|\.identityservice)[0m
[30;1m68 | [0m[35m-----------------------------------[0m
[30;1m69 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m70 | [0m[35mIt's a common misconception that, because a user can log in to your website[0m
[30;1m71 | [0m[35musing OAuth instead of creating a new username/password combination,[0m
[30;1m72 | [0m[35mthat means they do not have a user account on your website. This is false.[0m
[30;1m73 | [0m[35mLogging in with OAuth *does create a local user account*, and that user account[0m
[30;1m74 | [0m[35mwill have some kind of identifier (or ``user_id``). The ``user_id`` on this[0m

[31m--[ [0m[34mMatch #[0m[33m115[0m[34m of [0m[33m516[0m[31m ]--[0m
   Rule Id: [34mBD000701[0m
       Tag: [34mSecurity.Backdoor.DataExfiltration.Token[0m
  Severity: [36mImportant[0m, Confidence: [36mHigh[0m
  Filename: [33m/flask_dance-7.1.0/docs/concepts.rst[0m
   Pattern: [32m(npm owner|password|htpasswd|auth_?token|secret_?key|private_?key|authorized_keys?|npmrc|\.ssh|usersecrets?|api_?keys|nuget\.config|\.identityservice)[0m
[30;1m48 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m49 | [0m[35mThe most well-known use for OAuth is for bypassing user registration:[0m
[30;1m50 | [0m[35musers can "sign in" with a well-known OAuth provider like Google or Facebook[0m
[30;1m51 | [0m[35min order to avoid creating another username and password. However, this is[0m
[30;1m52 | [0m[35mnot the *only* use for OAuth. In fact, it's entirely possible to use[0m
